<li id="cite_note-Britannica-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Britannica_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/science/silicon" rel="nofollow">"Silicon"</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Britannica" title="Encyclopedia Britannica">Encyclopedia Britannica</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 August</span> 2019</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Encyclopedia+Britannica&amp;rft.atitle=Silicon&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2Fscience%2Fsilicon&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In his table of the elements, Lavoisier listed five "salifiable earths" (i.e., ores that could be made to react with acids to produce salts (<i>salis</i> = salt, in Latin): <i>chaux</i> (calcium oxide), <i>magnésie</i> (magnesia, magnesium oxide), <i>baryte</i> (barium sulfate), <i>alumine</i> (alumina, aluminium oxide), and <i>silice</i> (silica, silicon dioxide). About these "elements", Lavoisier speculates: "We are probably only acquainted as yet with a part of the metallic substances existing in nature, as all those which have a stronger affinity to oxygen than carbon possesses, are incapable, hitherto, of being reduced to a metallic state, and consequently, being only presented to our observation under the form of oxyds, are confounded with earths. It is extremely probable that barytes, which we have just now arranged with earths, is in this situation; for in many experiments it exhibits properties nearly approaching to those of metallic bodies. It is even possible that all the substances we call earths may be only metallic oxyds, irreducible by any hitherto known process." – from <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLavoisier1799">Lavoisier (1799). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/elementschemist00kerrgoog/page/n217" rel="nofollow"><i>Elements of Chemistry</i></a>. Translated by Robert Kerr (4 ed.). Edinburgh, Scotland: William Creec. p. 218.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Elements+of+Chemistry&amp;rft.place=Edinburgh%2C+Scotland&amp;rft.pages=218&amp;rft.edition=4&amp;rft.pub=William+Creec&amp;rft.date=1799&amp;rft.au=Lavoisier&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Felementschemist00kerrgoog%2Fpage%2Fn217&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span> (The original passage appears in: <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLavoisier1789">Lavoisier (1789). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=hZch3yOrayUC&amp;pg=PA174" rel="nofollow"><i>Traité Élémentaire de Chimie</i></a>. Vol. 1. Paris, France: Cuchet. p. 174.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Trait%C3%A9+%C3%89l%C3%A9mentaire+de+Chimie&amp;rft.place=Paris%2C+France&amp;rft.pages=174&amp;rft.pub=Cuchet&amp;rft.date=1789&amp;rft.au=Lavoisier&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DhZch3yOrayUC%26pg%3DPA174&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328_14-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328_14-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328_14-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328_14-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenwoodEarnshaw1997328_14-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGreenwoodEarnshaw1997">Greenwood &amp; Earnshaw 1997</a>, p. 328.<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> sfn error: no target: CITEREFGreenwoodEarnshaw1997 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFDavy1808">Davy, Humphry (1808). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Kg9GAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA333" rel="nofollow">"Electro chemical researches, on the decomposition of the earths; with observations on the metals obtained from the alkaline earths, and on the amalgam procured from ammonia"</a>. <i>Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society of London</i>. W. Bowyer and J. Nichols. <b>98</b>: 333–370.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Philosophical+Transactions+of+the+Royal+Society+of+London&amp;rft.atitle=Electro+chemical+researches%2C+on+the+decomposition+of+the+earths%3B+with+observations+on+the+metals+obtained+from+the+alkaline+earths%2C+and+on+the+amalgam+procured+from+ammonia&amp;rft.volume=98&amp;rft.pages=333-370&amp;rft.date=1808&amp;rft.aulast=Davy&amp;rft.aufirst=Humphry&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DKg9GAAAAMAAJ%26pg%3DPA333&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span>. On <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Kg9GAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA353" rel="nofollow">p. 353</a> Davy coins the name "silicium" : "Had I been so fortunate as to have obtained more certain evidences on this subject, and to have procured the metallic substances I was in search of, I should have proposed for them the names of silicium [silicon], alumium [aluminium], zirconium, and glucium [beryllium]."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFThomsonBaldwinBlackwoodBaldwin1817">Thomson, Thomas; Baldwin, Charles; Blackwood, William; Baldwin, Cradock; Bell &amp; Bradfute, bookseller; Hodges &amp; McArthur, bookseller (1817). <a class="external text" href="http://archive.org/details/bub_gb_zVA0AQAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>A system of chemistry : in four volumes</i></a>. University of Wisconsin - Madison. London : Printed for Baldwin, Craddock, and Joy, Paternoster-Row; William Blackwood, and Bell and Bradfute, Edinburgh; and Hodges and Macarthur, Dublin. p. 252.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+system+of+chemistry+%3A+in+four+volumes&amp;rft.pages=252&amp;rft.pub=London+%3A+Printed+for+Baldwin%2C+Craddock%2C+and+Joy%2C+Paternoster-Row%3B+William+Blackwood%2C+and+Bell+and+Bradfute%2C+Edinburgh%3B+and+Hodges+and+Macarthur%2C+Dublin&amp;rft.date=1817&amp;rft.aulast=Thomson&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas&amp;rft.au=Baldwin%2C+Charles&amp;rft.au=Blackwood%2C+William&amp;rft.au=Baldwin%2C+Cradock&amp;rft.au=Bell+%26+Bradfute%2C+bookseller&amp;rft.au=Hodges+%26+McArthur%2C+bookseller&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fbub_gb_zVA0AQAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span>: "The base of silica has been usually considered as a metal, and called <i>silicium</i>. But as there is not the smallest evidence for its metallic nature, and as it bears a close resemblance to boron and carbon, it is better to class it along with these bodies, and to give it the name of <i>silicon</i>."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See
<ul><li>Berzelius announced his discovery of silicon ("silicium") in: Berzelius, J. (presented: 1823; published: 1824) <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pJlPAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA46" rel="nofollow">"Undersökning af flusspatssyran och dess märkvärdigaste föreningar"</a> (Investigation of hydrofluoric acid and of its most noteworthy compounds), <i>Kongliga Vetenskaps-Academiens Handlingar</i> [Proceedings of the Royal Science Academy], <b>12</b> : 46–98. The isolation of silicon and its characterization are detailed in the section titled "Flussspatssyrad kisseljords sönderdelning med kalium," pp. 46–68.</li>
<li>The above article was printed in German in: J.J. Berzelius (1824) <a class="external text" href="http://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k15086x/f185.image.langEN" rel="nofollow">"<i>II. Untersuchungen über Flussspathsäure und deren merkwürdigsten Verbindungen</i>"</a> (II. Investigations of hydrofluoric acid and its most noteworthy compounds), <i>Annalen der Physik</i>, <b>77</b>: 169–230. The isolation of silicon is detailed in the section titled: <a class="external text" href="http://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k15086x/f220.image.langEN" rel="nofollow">"Zersetzung der flussspaths. Kieselerde durch Kalium"</a> (Decomposition of silicate fluoride by potassium), pp. 204–210.</li>
<li>The above article was reprinted in French in: Berzelius (1824) <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=eHmstO7CmqAC&amp;pg=PA337" rel="nofollow">"Décomposition du fluate de silice par le potassium"</a> (Decomposition of silica fluoride by potassium), <i>Annales de Chimie et de Physique</i>, <b>27</b>: 337–359.</li>
<li>Reprinted in English in: <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_UwwAAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA254" rel="nofollow">"On the mode of obtaining silicium, and on the characters and properties of that substance"</a>. <i>The Philosophical Magazine and Journal: Comprehending Various Branches of Science, the Liberal and Fine Arts, Agriculture, Manufactures, and Commerce</i>. Richard Taylor and Company. <b>65</b>: 254–267. 1825.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Philosophical+Magazine+and+Journal%3A+Comprehending+Various+Branches+of+Science%2C+the+Liberal+and+Fine+Arts%2C+Agriculture%2C+Manufactures%2C+and+Commerce&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+mode+of+obtaining+silicium%2C+and+on+the+characters+and+properties+of+that+substance&amp;rft.volume=65&amp;rft.pages=254-267&amp;rft.date=1825&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D_UwwAAAAIAAJ%26pg%3DPA254&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFWeeks1932"><a href="/wiki/Mary_Elvira_Weeks" title="Mary Elvira Weeks">Weeks, Mary Elvira</a> (1932). "The discovery of the elements: XII. Other elements isolated with the aid of potassium and sodium: beryllium, boron, silicon, and aluminum". <i>Journal of Chemical Education</i>. <b>9</b> (8): 1386–1412. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1932JChEd...9.1386W" rel="nofollow">1932JChEd...9.1386W</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1021%2Fed009p1386" rel="nofollow">10.1021/ed009p1386</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Chemical+Education&amp;rft.atitle=The+discovery+of+the+elements%3A+XII.+Other+elements+isolated+with+the+aid+of+potassium+and+sodium%3A+beryllium%2C+boron%2C+silicon%2C+and+aluminum&amp;rft.volume=9&amp;rft.issue=8&amp;rft.pages=1386-1412&amp;rft.date=1932&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1021%2Fed009p1386&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1932JChEd...9.1386W&amp;rft.aulast=Weeks&amp;rft.aufirst=Mary+Elvira&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFVoronkov2007">Voronkov, M.G. (2007). "Silicon era". <i>Russian Journal of Applied Chemistry</i>. <b>80</b> (12): 2190. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1134%2FS1070427207120397" rel="nofollow">10.1134/S1070427207120397</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:195240638" rel="nofollow">195240638</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Russian+Journal+of+Applied+Chemistry&amp;rft.atitle=Silicon+era&amp;rft.volume=80&amp;rft.issue=12&amp;rft.pages=2190&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1134%2FS1070427207120397&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A195240638%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.aulast=Voronkov&amp;rft.aufirst=M.G.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1854, Deville was trying to prepare aluminium metal from aluminium chloride that was heavily contaminated with silicon chloride. Deville used two methods to prepare aluminium: heating aluminium chloride with sodium metal in an inert atmosphere (of hydrogen); and melting aluminum chloride with sodium chloride and then electrolyzing the mixture. In both cases, pure silicon was produced: the silicon dissolved in the molten aluminium, but crystallized upon cooling. Dissolving the crude aluminum in hydrochloric acid revealed flakes of crystallized silicon. See: Henri Sainte-Claire Deville (1854) <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=C3VFAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA321" rel="nofollow">"Note sur deux procédés de préparation de l'aluminium et sur une nouvelle forme du silicium"</a> (Note on two procedures for the preparation of aluminium and on a new form of silicon), <i>Comptes rendus</i>, <b>39</b>: 321–326.<br/>Subsequently, Deville obtained crystalline silicon by heating the chloride or fluoride of silicon with sodium metal, isolating the amorphous silicon, then melting the amorphous form with salt and heating the mixture until most of the salt evaporated. See: <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSainte-Claire_Deville1855">Sainte-Claire Deville, H. (1855). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=tZhDAQAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA1034" rel="nofollow">"Du silicium et du titane (On silicon and titanium)"</a>. <i>Comptes rendus</i>. <b>40</b>: 1034–1036.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Comptes+rendus&amp;rft.atitle=Du+silicium+et+du+titane+%28On+silicon+and+titanium%29&amp;rft.volume=40&amp;rft.pages=1034-1036&amp;rft.date=1855&amp;rft.aulast=Sainte-Claire+Deville&amp;rft.aufirst=H.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DtZhDAQAAIAAJ%26pg%3DPA1034&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASilicon"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://ww1.etacude.com/" rel="nofollow">"Information on silicon – history, thermodynamic, chemical, physical and electronic properties"</a>. <i>Etacude</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
